<p>The <b>African Union</b> (<b>AU</b>) is a <a href="/wiki/Continental_union" title="Continental union">continental union</a> consisting of 54 <a href="/wiki/Sovereign_state" title="Sovereign state">countries</a> in Africa. The only African state that is not a member is <a href="/wiki/Morocco" title="Morocco">Morocco</a>, although <a href="/wiki/Burkina_Faso" title="Burkina Faso">Burkina Faso</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Central_African_Republic" title="Central African Republic">Central African Republic</a> have had their memberships suspended due to the <a href="/wiki/2015_Burkinab%C3%A9_coup_d%27%C3%A9tat" title="2015 Burkinabé coup d'état" class="mw-redirect">recent coup d'état</a> and <a href="/wiki/Central_African_Republic_conflict_(2012%E2%80%93present)" title="Central African Republic conflict (2012–present)" class="mw-redirect">ongoing civil war</a> respectively. The AU was established on 26 May 2001 in <a href="/wiki/Addis_Ababa" title="Addis Ababa">Addis Ababa</a> and launched on 9 July 2002 in South Africa,<sup id="cite_ref-African_Union_2002_6-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-African_Union_2002-6"><span>[</span>6<span>]</span></a></sup> with the aim of replacing the <a href="/wiki/Organisation_of_African_Unity" title="Organisation of African Unity">Organisation of African Unity</a> (OAU). The most important decisions of the AU are made by the <a href="/wiki/Assembly_of_the_African_Union" title="Assembly of the African Union">Assembly of the African Union</a>, a semi-annual meeting of the heads of state and government of its member states. The AU's secretariat, the <a href="/wiki/African_Union_Commission" title="African Union Commission">African Union Commission</a>, is based in <a href="/wiki/Addis_Ababa" title="Addis Ababa">Addis Ababa</a>, Ethiopia.</p>
<p></p>

<p></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Overview">Overview</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=African_Union&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Overview">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>The objectives of the AU are:</p>
<ol>
<li>To achieve greater unity and solidarity between the African countries and Africans.</li>
<li>To defend the sovereignty, <a href="/wiki/Territorial_integrity" title="Territorial integrity">territorial integrity</a> and independence of its Member States.</li>
<li>To accelerate the political and social-economic integration of the continent.</li>
<li>To promote and defend African common positions on issues of interest to the continent and its peoples.</li>
<li>To encourage international cooperation, taking due account of the <a href="/wiki/Charter_of_the_United_Nations" title="Charter of the United Nations" class="mw-redirect">Charter of the United Nations</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Universal_Declaration_of_Human_Rights" title="Universal Declaration of Human Rights">Universal Declaration of Human Rights</a>.</li>
<li>To promote peace, security, and stability on the continent.</li>
<li>To promote democratic principles and institutions, popular participation and good governance.</li>
<li>To promote and protect human and peoples' rights in accordance with the <a href="/wiki/African_Charter_on_Human_and_Peoples%27_Rights" title="African Charter on Human and Peoples' Rights">African Charter on Human and Peoples' Rights</a> and other relevant <a href="/wiki/International_human_rights_instruments" title="International human rights instruments">human rights instruments</a>.</li>
<li>To establish the necessary conditions which enable the continent to play its rightful role in the global economy and in international negotiations.</li>
<li>To promote <a href="/wiki/Sustainable_development" title="Sustainable development">sustainable development</a> at the <a href="/wiki/Economic,_social_and_cultural_rights" title="Economic, social and cultural rights">economic, social and cultural levels</a> as well as the integration of African economies.</li>
<li>To promote co-operation in all fields of human activity to raise the <a href="/wiki/Living_standard" title="Living standard" class="mw-redirect">living standards</a> of African peoples.</li>
<li>To coordinate and harmonize the policies between the existing and future <a href="/wiki/Regional_Economic_Communities" title="Regional Economic Communities">Regional Economic Communities</a> for the gradual attainment of the objectives of the Union.</li>
<li>To advance the development of the continent by promoting research in all fields, in particular in science and technology.</li>
<li>To work with relevant international partners in the eradication of preventable diseases and the promotion of good health on the continent.</li>
</ol>
<p>The African Union is made up of both political and administrative bodies. The highest decision-making organ is the <a href="/wiki/Assembly_of_the_African_Union" title="Assembly of the African Union">Assembly of the African Union</a>, made up of all the heads of state or government of member states of the AU. The Assembly is chaired by <a href="/wiki/Robert_Mugabe" title="Robert Mugabe">Robert Mugabe</a>, President of <a href="/wiki/Zimbabwe" title="Zimbabwe">Zimbabwe</a>. The AU also has a representative body, the <a href="/wiki/Pan_African_Parliament" title="Pan African Parliament" class="mw-redirect">Pan African Parliament</a>, which consists of 265 members elected by the national legislatures of the AU member states. Its president is <a href="/wiki/Bethel_Nnaemeka_Amadi" title="Bethel Nnaemeka Amadi">Bethel Nnaemeka Amadi</a>.</p>
<p>Other political institutions of the AU include</p>
<ul>
<li>the <a href="/wiki/Executive_Council_of_the_African_Union" title="Executive Council of the African Union">Executive Council</a>, made up of <a href="/wiki/Foreign_minister" title="Foreign minister">foreign ministers</a>, which prepares decisions for the Assembly;</li>
<li>the <a href="/w/index.php?title=Permanent_Representatives_Committee&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Permanent Representatives Committee (page does not exist)">Permanent Representatives Committee</a>, made up of the ambassadors to <a href="/wiki/Addis_Ababa" title="Addis Ababa">Addis Ababa</a> of AU member states; and</li>
<li>the <a href="/wiki/Economic,_Social,_and_Cultural_Council" title="Economic, Social, and Cultural Council" class="mw-redirect">Economic, Social, and Cultural Council</a> (ECOSOCC), a civil society consultative body.</li>
</ul>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/African_Union_Commission" title="African Union Commission">AU Commission</a>, the secretariat to the political structures, is chaired by <a href="/wiki/Nkosazana_Dlamini-Zuma" title="Nkosazana Dlamini-Zuma">Nkosazana Dlamini-Zuma</a> of South Africa. On 15 July 2012, Ms. Dlamini-Zuma won a tightly contested vote to become the first female head of the African Union Commission, replacing <a href="/wiki/Jean_Ping" title="Jean Ping">Jean Ping</a> of <a href="/wiki/Gabon" title="Gabon">Gabon</a>.</p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;"><a href="/wiki/File:African_Union_conference_center_and_office_complex,_AUCC.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7e/African_Union_conference_center_and_office_complex%2C_AUCC.jpg/250px-African_Union_conference_center_and_office_complex%2C_AUCC.jpg" width="250" height="185" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7e/African_Union_conference_center_and_office_complex%2C_AUCC.jpg/375px-African_Union_conference_center_and_office_complex%2C_AUCC.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7e/African_Union_conference_center_and_office_complex%2C_AUCC.jpg/500px-African_Union_conference_center_and_office_complex%2C_AUCC.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2686" data-file-height="1988" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:African_Union_conference_center_and_office_complex,_AUCC.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The African Union's headquarters complex in <a href="/wiki/Addis_Ababa" title="Addis Ababa">Addis Ababa</a>.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The main administrative capital of the African Union is in <a href="/wiki/Addis_Ababa" title="Addis Ababa">Addis Ababa</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ethiopia" title="Ethiopia">Ethiopia</a>, where the <a href="/wiki/African_Union_Commission" title="African Union Commission">African Union Commission</a> is headquartered. A new headquarters complex, the <a href="/wiki/AU_Conference_Center_and_Office_Complex" title="AU Conference Center and Office Complex">AU Conference Center and Office Complex</a> (AUCC), was inaugurated on 28 January 2012, during the 18th AU summit.<sup id="cite_ref-AU_NewHQ_7-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AU_NewHQ-7"><span>[</span>7<span>]</span></a></sup> The complex was built by <a href="/wiki/China_State_Construction_Engineering_Corporation" title="China State Construction Engineering Corporation" class="mw-redirect">China State Construction Engineering Corporation</a> as a gift from the <a href="/wiki/Government_of_the_People%27s_Republic_of_China" title="Government of the People's Republic of China" class="mw-redirect">Chinese government</a>, and accommodates, amongst other facilities, a 2,500-seat plenary hall and a 20-story office tower. The tower is 99.9 meters high to signify the date 9 September 1999, when the <a href="/wiki/Organization_of_African_Unity" title="Organization of African Unity" class="mw-redirect">Organization of African Unity</a> voted to become the African Union.<sup id="cite_ref-Chinadaily_NewHQ_8-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Chinadaily_NewHQ-8"><span>[</span>8<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Other AU structures are hosted by different member states:</p>
<ul>
<li>the <a href="/wiki/African_Commission_on_Human_and_Peoples%27_Rights" title="African Commission on Human and Peoples' Rights">African Commission on Human and Peoples' Rights</a> is based in <a href="/wiki/Banjul" title="Banjul">Banjul</a>, <a href="/wiki/The_Gambia" title="The Gambia">the Gambia</a>; and</li>
<li>the <a href="/wiki/New_Partnership_for_Africa%27s_Development" title="New Partnership for Africa's Development">New Partnership for Africa's Development</a> (NEPAD) and <a href="/wiki/APRM" title="APRM" class="mw-redirect">APRM</a> <a href="//en.wiktionary.org/wiki/secretariat" class="extiw" title="wikt:secretariat">Secretariats</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Pan-African_Parliament" title="Pan-African Parliament">Pan-African Parliament</a> are in <a href="/wiki/Midrand" title="Midrand">Midrand</a>, South Africa.</li>
</ul>
<p>The AU covers the entire continent except for <a href="/wiki/Morocco" title="Morocco">Morocco</a> and several territories held by Spain (<a href="/wiki/Canary_Islands" title="Canary Islands">Canary Islands</a>), France (<a href="/wiki/Mayotte" title="Mayotte">Mayotte</a>, <a href="/wiki/R%C3%A9union" title="Réunion">Réunion</a>, <a href="/wiki/Scattered_Islands_in_the_Indian_Ocean" title="Scattered Islands in the Indian Ocean">Scattered Islands in the Indian Ocean</a>), Portugal (<a href="/wiki/Madeira" title="Madeira">Madeira</a>, <a href="/wiki/Savage_Islands" title="Savage Islands">Savage Islands</a>) and the United Kingdom, <a href="/wiki/Saint_Helena,_Ascension_and_Tristan_da_Cunha" title="Saint Helena, Ascension and Tristan da Cunha">Saint Helena, Ascension and Tristan da Cunha</a>)<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Avoid_weasel_words" title="Wikipedia:Avoid weasel words" class="mw-redirect"><span title="The material near this tag possibly uses too vague attribution or weasel words. (September 2014)">which?</span></a></i>]</sup>. Morocco is not a member because its government opposes the membership of <a href="/wiki/Western_Sahara" title="Western Sahara">Western Sahara</a> as the <a href="/wiki/Sahrawi_Arab_Democratic_Republic" title="Sahrawi Arab Democratic Republic">Sahrawi Arab Democratic Republic</a>. However, Morocco has a special status within the AU and benefits from the services available to all AU states from the institutions of the AU, such as the <a href="/wiki/African_Development_Bank" title="African Development Bank">African Development Bank</a>. Moroccan delegates also participate at important AU functions, and negotiations continue to try to resolve the conflict with the <a href="/wiki/Polisario_Front" title="Polisario Front">Polisario Front</a> in <a href="/wiki/Tindouf" title="Tindouf">Tindouf</a>, <a href="/wiki/Algeria" title="Algeria">Algeria</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Free_Zone_(Western_Sahara_region)" title="Free Zone (Western Sahara region)" class="mw-redirect">parts of Western Sahara</a>.</p>
<p>The AU's first military intervention in a member state was the May 2003 deployment of a peacekeeping force of soldiers from South Africa, <a href="/wiki/Ethiopia" title="Ethiopia">Ethiopia</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Mozambique" title="Mozambique">Mozambique</a> to <a href="/wiki/Burundi" title="Burundi">Burundi</a> to oversee the implementation of the various agreements. AU troops were also deployed in <a href="/wiki/Sudan" title="Sudan">Sudan</a> for peacekeeping in the <a href="/wiki/Darfur_conflict" title="Darfur conflict" class="mw-redirect">Darfur conflict</a>, before the mission was handed over to the United Nations on 1 January 2008 <a href="/wiki/UNAMID" title="UNAMID" class="mw-redirect">UNAMID</a>. The AU has also sent a peacekeeping mission to <a href="/wiki/Somalia" title="Somalia">Somalia</a>, of which the peacekeeping troops are from <a href="/wiki/Uganda" title="Uganda">Uganda</a> and <a href="/wiki/Burundi" title="Burundi">Burundi</a>.</p>
<p>The AU has adopted a number of important new documents establishing norms at continental level, to supplement those already in force when it was created. These include the <a href="/wiki/African_Union_Convention_on_Preventing_and_Combating_Corruption" title="African Union Convention on Preventing and Combating Corruption">African Union Convention on Preventing and Combating Corruption</a> (2003), the <a href="/w/index.php?title=African_Charter_on_Democracy,_Elections_and_Governance&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="African Charter on Democracy, Elections and Governance (page does not exist)">African Charter on Democracy, Elections and Governance</a> (2007), the <a href="/wiki/New_Partnership_for_Africa%27s_Development" title="New Partnership for Africa's Development">New Partnership for Africa's Development</a> (NEPAD) and its associated Declaration on Democracy, Political, Economic and Corporate Governance.<sup id="cite_ref-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-9"><span>[</span>9<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Treaties">Treaties</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=African_Union&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Treaties">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Membership">Membership</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=African_Union&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Membership">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="hatnote">See also: <a href="/wiki/Member_states_of_the_African_Union" title="Member states of the African Union">Member states of the African Union</a></div>
<p>All <a href="/wiki/UN_member_states" title="UN member states" class="mw-redirect">UN member states</a> based in Africa and African waters are or have been members of the AU or OAU, as is the <a href="/wiki/Sahrawi_Arab_Democratic_Republic" title="Sahrawi Arab Democratic Republic">Sahrawi Arab Democratic Republic</a>, whose <a href="/wiki/International_recognition_of_the_Sahrawi_Arab_Democratic_Republic" title="International recognition of the Sahrawi Arab Democratic Republic">status is disputed</a>. Morocco unilaterally withdrew, while <a href="/wiki/Burkina_Faso" title="Burkina Faso">Burkina Faso</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Central_African_Republic" title="Central African Republic">Central African Republic</a> are currently suspended. Spain, primarily a European country, maintains sovereignty over <a href="/wiki/Ceuta" title="Ceuta">Ceuta</a> and <a href="/wiki/Melilla" title="Melilla">Melilla</a> on the African mainland and the <a href="/wiki/Canary_Islands" title="Canary Islands">Canary Islands</a>, and is accredited to the African Union.<sup id="cite_ref-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10"><span>[</span>10<span>]</span></a></sup></p>

<li><span class="flagicon"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6a/Flag_of_Zimbabwe.svg/23px-Flag_of_Zimbabwe.svg.png" width="23" height="12" class="thumbborder" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6a/Flag_of_Zimbabwe.svg/35px-Flag_of_Zimbabwe.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6a/Flag_of_Zimbabwe.svg/46px-Flag_of_Zimbabwe.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="1200" data-file-height="600" />&#160;</span><a href="/wiki/Zimbabwe" title="Zimbabwe">Zimbabwe</a></li>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Suspended_members">Suspended members</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=African_Union&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Suspended members">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Regions_of_the_African_Union.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/17/Regions_of_the_African_Union.png/220px-Regions_of_the_African_Union.png" width="220" height="220" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/17/Regions_of_the_African_Union.png/330px-Regions_of_the_African_Union.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/17/Regions_of_the_African_Union.png/440px-Regions_of_the_African_Union.png 2x" data-file-width="2000" data-file-height="2000" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Regions_of_the_African_Union.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Regions_of_the_African_Union" title="Regions of the African Union">Regions of the African Union</a><br />
<span style="background-color:#DAA520; color:; border:1px solid darkgray; text-align:center;">&#160;North&#160;</span> <span style="background-color:#87CEEB; color:; border:1px solid darkgray; text-align:center;">&#160;Southern&#160;</span> <span style="background-color:#90EE90; color:; border:1px solid darkgray; text-align:center;">&#160;East&#160;</span> <span style="background-color:#FA8072; color:; border:1px solid darkgray; text-align:center;">&#160;West&#160;</span> <span style="background-color:#7B68EE; color:; border:1px solid darkgray; text-align:center;">&#160;Central&#160;</span></div>
</div>
</div>
<ul>
<li><span class="flagicon"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/31/Flag_of_Burkina_Faso.svg/23px-Flag_of_Burkina_Faso.svg.png" width="23" height="15" class="thumbborder" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/31/Flag_of_Burkina_Faso.svg/35px-Flag_of_Burkina_Faso.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/31/Flag_of_Burkina_Faso.svg/45px-Flag_of_Burkina_Faso.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="900" data-file-height="600" />&#160;</span><a href="/wiki/Burkina_Faso" title="Burkina Faso">Burkina Faso</a>&#160;– suspended after the <a href="/wiki/2015_Burkinab%C3%A9_coup_d%27%C3%A9tat" title="2015 Burkinabé coup d'état" class="mw-redirect">2015 Burkinabé coup d'état</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-11"><span>[</span>11<span>]</span></a></sup></li>
<li><span class="flagicon"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6f/Flag_of_the_Central_African_Republic.svg/23px-Flag_of_the_Central_African_Republic.svg.png" width="23" height="15" class="thumbborder" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6f/Flag_of_the_Central_African_Republic.svg/35px-Flag_of_the_Central_African_Republic.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6f/Flag_of_the_Central_African_Republic.svg/45px-Flag_of_the_Central_African_Republic.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="450" data-file-height="300" />&#160;</span><a href="/wiki/Central_African_Republic" title="Central African Republic">Central African Republic</a>&#160;– suspended due to the <a href="/wiki/Central_African_Republic_conflict_(2012%E2%80%93present)" title="Central African Republic conflict (2012–present)" class="mw-redirect">Central African Republic conflict</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-12"><span>[</span>12<span>]</span></a></sup></li>
</ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Member_observer">Member observer</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=African_Union&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Member observer">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<ul>
<li><span class="flagicon"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/56/Flag_of_Haiti.svg/23px-Flag_of_Haiti.svg.png" width="23" height="14" class="thumbborder" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/56/Flag_of_Haiti.svg/35px-Flag_of_Haiti.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/56/Flag_of_Haiti.svg/46px-Flag_of_Haiti.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="500" data-file-height="300" />&#160;</span><a href="/wiki/Haiti" title="Haiti">Haiti</a> – At the 18th AU summit in Addis Ababa on 2 February 2012, Haiti obtained <a href="/wiki/Observer_status" title="Observer status">Member Observer</a> status and thereafter submitted a formal request to become an Associate Member.<sup id="cite_ref-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-13"><span>[</span>13<span>]</span></a></sup></li>
<li><span class="flagicon"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d3/Flag_of_Kazakhstan.svg/23px-Flag_of_Kazakhstan.svg.png" width="23" height="12" class="thumbborder" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d3/Flag_of_Kazakhstan.svg/35px-Flag_of_Kazakhstan.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d3/Flag_of_Kazakhstan.svg/46px-Flag_of_Kazakhstan.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="600" data-file-height="300" />&#160;</span><a href="/wiki/Kazakhstan" title="Kazakhstan">Kazakhstan</a> – On 14 November 2013, Kazakhstan obtained <a href="/wiki/Observer_status" title="Observer status">Member Observer</a> status after the appropriate treaties were ratified in May 2013. Foreign Minister <a href="/wiki/Erlan_Idrisov" title="Erlan Idrisov" class="mw-redirect">Erlan Idrisov</a> became the Permanent Representative of the Republic of Kazakhstan in the African Union.<sup id="cite_ref-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-14"><span>[</span>14<span>]</span></a></sup></li>
<li><span class="flagicon"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/84/Flag_of_Latvia.svg/23px-Flag_of_Latvia.svg.png" width="23" height="12" class="thumbborder" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/84/Flag_of_Latvia.svg/35px-Flag_of_Latvia.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/84/Flag_of_Latvia.svg/46px-Flag_of_Latvia.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="1200" data-file-height="600" />&#160;</span><a href="/wiki/Latvia" title="Latvia">Latvia</a> – Observer state to the African Union since 2012.<sup id="cite_ref-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15"><span>[</span>15<span>]</span></a></sup></li>
<li><span class="flagicon"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/00/Flag_of_Palestine.svg/23px-Flag_of_Palestine.svg.png" width="23" height="12" class="thumbborder" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/00/Flag_of_Palestine.svg/35px-Flag_of_Palestine.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/00/Flag_of_Palestine.svg/46px-Flag_of_Palestine.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="1200" data-file-height="600" />&#160;</span><a href="/wiki/State_of_Palestine" title="State of Palestine">Palestine</a> – At the 21st summit of the African Union organization granted Palestine observer status.<sup id="cite_ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16"><span>[</span>16<span>]</span></a></sup></li>
<li><span class="flagicon"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/ff/Flag_of_Serbia.svg/23px-Flag_of_Serbia.svg.png" width="23" height="15" class="thumbborder" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/ff/Flag_of_Serbia.svg/35px-Flag_of_Serbia.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/ff/Flag_of_Serbia.svg/45px-Flag_of_Serbia.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="1350" data-file-height="900" />&#160;</span><a href="/wiki/Serbia" title="Serbia">Serbia</a> – country has <a href="/wiki/Observer_status" title="Observer status">Member Observer</a> status in African Union and <a href="/wiki/Minister_of_Foreign_Affairs_(Serbia)" title="Minister of Foreign Affairs (Serbia)">Serbian Foreign Ministers</a> <a href="/wiki/Ivan_Mrki%C4%87" title="Ivan Mrkić">Ivan Mrkić</a> in 2012 and 2014 and <a href="/wiki/Vuk_Jeremi%C4%87" title="Vuk Jeremić">Vuk Jeremić</a> in 2011 participated in Addis Ababa Summits.<sup id="cite_ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17"><span>[</span>17<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18"><span>[</span>18<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19"><span>[</span>19<span>]</span></a></sup></li>
<li><span class="flagicon"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b4/Flag_of_Turkey.svg/23px-Flag_of_Turkey.svg.png" width="23" height="15" class="thumbborder" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b4/Flag_of_Turkey.svg/35px-Flag_of_Turkey.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b4/Flag_of_Turkey.svg/45px-Flag_of_Turkey.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="1200" data-file-height="800" />&#160;</span><a href="/wiki/Turkey" title="Turkey">Turkey</a> – country has <a href="/wiki/Observer_status" title="Observer status">Member Observer</a> status since 2005.<sup id="cite_ref-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20"><span>[</span>20<span>]</span></a></sup></li>
</ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Former_members">Former members</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=African_Union&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Former members">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<ul>
<li><span class="flagicon"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2c/Flag_of_Morocco.svg/23px-Flag_of_Morocco.svg.png" width="23" height="15" class="thumbborder" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2c/Flag_of_Morocco.svg/35px-Flag_of_Morocco.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2c/Flag_of_Morocco.svg/45px-Flag_of_Morocco.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="900" data-file-height="600" />&#160;</span><a href="/wiki/Morocco" title="Morocco">Morocco</a> – left the AU's predecessor, the <a href="/wiki/Organisation_of_African_Unity" title="Organisation of African Unity">Organisation of African Unity</a> (OAU) in 1984, when the majority of member countries supported the <a href="/wiki/Sahrawi_Arab_Democratic_Republic" title="Sahrawi Arab Democratic Republic">Sahrawi Arab Democratic Republic</a> (proclaimed by the <a href="/wiki/Polisario_Front" title="Polisario Front">Polisario Front</a> in 1976 claiming the representation of the <a href="/wiki/Western_Sahara" title="Western Sahara">Western Sahara</a>), resulting on SADR admission in the AU.<sup id="cite_ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21"><span>[</span>21<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22"><span>[</span>22<span>]</span></a></sup> Morocco's ally, <a href="/wiki/Zaire" title="Zaire">Zaire</a> (now the <a href="/wiki/Democratic_Republic_of_the_Congo" title="Democratic Republic of the Congo">Democratic Republic of the Congo</a>), similarly opposed the OAU's admission of the Sahrawi Republic, and the <a href="/wiki/Mobutu_Sese_Seko" title="Mobutu Sese Seko">Mobutu</a> regime boycotted the organisation from 1984 to 1986.<sup id="cite_ref-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-23"><span>[</span>23<span>]</span></a></sup> Some countries have since <a href="/wiki/Foreign_relations_of_the_Sahrawi_Republic#States_suspending_relations_with_the_Sahrawi_Arab_Democratic_Republic" title="Foreign relations of the Sahrawi Republic" class="mw-redirect">retracted their support</a> for the Sahrawi Republic.</li>
</ul>

<dl>

</dl>
</dd>
</dl>
</td>
</tr>

<div class="plainlinks hlist navbar mini">
<ul>
<li class="nv-view"><a href="/wiki/Template:Politics_of_the_African_Union" title="Template:Politics of the African Union"><span title="View this template">v</span></a></li>
<li class="nv-talk"><a href="/wiki/Template_talk:Politics_of_the_African_Union" title="Template talk:Politics of the African Union"><span title="Discuss this template">t</span></a></li>
<li class="nv-edit"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Template:Politics_of_the_African_Union&amp;action=edit"><span title="Edit this template">e</span></a></li>
</ul>
</div>

</table>
<p>The African Union has a number of official bodies:</p>
<dl>
<dt><a href="/wiki/Pan-African_Parliament" title="Pan-African Parliament">Pan-African Parliament</a> (PAP)</dt>
<dd>To become the highest legislative body of the African Union. The seat of the PAP is at <a href="/wiki/Midrand" title="Midrand">Midrand</a>, South Africa. The Parliament is composed of 265&#160;elected representatives from all 54&#160;AU states, and intended to provide popular and civil-society participation in the processes of democratic governance. Its president is the Hon. Prince <a href="/wiki/Bethel_Nnaemeka_Amadi" title="Bethel Nnaemeka Amadi">Bethel Nnaemeka Amadi</a>, Esq. of <a href="/wiki/Nigeria" title="Nigeria">Nigeria</a>.</dd>
</dl>
<dl>
<dt><a href="/wiki/Assembly_of_the_African_Union" title="Assembly of the African Union">Assembly of the African Union</a></dt>
<dd>Composed of heads of state and heads of government of AU states, the Assembly is currently the supreme governing body of the African Union. It is gradually devolving some of its decision-making powers to the Pan African Parliament. It meets once a year and makes its decisions by consensus or by a two-thirds majority. The current <a href="/wiki/Chairperson_of_the_African_Union" title="Chairperson of the African Union">chair of the AU</a> is <a href="/wiki/Zimbabwe" title="Zimbabwe">Zimbabwean</a> President <a href="/wiki/Robert_Mugabe" title="Robert Mugabe">Robert Mugabe</a>.</dd>
</dl>
<dl>
<dt><a href="/wiki/African_Union_Commission" title="African Union Commission">African Union Commission (or Authority)</a>&#160;</dt>
<dd>The secretariat of the African Union, composed of ten commissioners and supporting staff and headquartered in <a href="/wiki/Addis_Ababa" title="Addis Ababa">Addis Ababa</a>, Ethiopia. In a similar fashion to its <a href="/wiki/European_Union" title="European Union">European</a> counterpart, the <a href="/wiki/European_Commission" title="European Commission">European Commission</a>, it is responsible for the administration and co-ordination of the AU's activities and meetings.</dd>
</dl>
<dl>
<dt><a href="/wiki/African_Court_of_Justice" title="African Court of Justice">African Court of Justice</a></dt>
<dd>The Constitutive Act provides for a Court of Justice to rule on disputes over interpretation of AU treaties. A protocol to set up the Court of Justice was adopted in 2003 and entered into force in 2009. It is likely to be superseded by a protocol creating a Court of Justice and Human Rights, which will incorporate the already established African Court of Justice and Human and Peoples' Rights (see below) and have two chambers—one for general legal matters and one for rulings on the human rights treaties.</dd>
</dl>
<dl>
<dt><a href="/wiki/Executive_Council_of_the_African_Union" title="Executive Council of the African Union">Executive Council</a></dt>
<dd>Composed of ministers designated by the governments of member states. It decides on matters such as foreign trade, social security, food, agriculture and communications, is accountable to the Assembly, and prepares material for the Assembly to discuss and approve.It is chaired by Mr Shawn Makuyana of Zimbabwe (2015–).</dd>
</dl>
<dl>
<dt><a href="/wiki/Permanent_Representatives%27_Committee_of_the_African_Union" title="Permanent Representatives' Committee of the African Union">Permanent Representatives' Committee</a></dt>
<dd>Consisting of nominated permanent representatives of member states, the Committee prepares the work for the Executive Council, similar the role of the <a href="/wiki/Committee_of_Permanent_Representatives" title="Committee of Permanent Representatives">Committee of Permanent Representatives</a> in the <a href="/wiki/European_Union" title="European Union">European Union</a>.</dd>
</dl>
<dl>
<dt><a href="/wiki/Peace_and_Security_Council" title="Peace and Security Council">Peace and Security Council</a> (PSC)</dt>
<dd>Proposed at the Lusaka Summit in 2001 and established in 2004 under a protocol to the Constitutive Act adopted by the AU Assembly in July 2002. The protocol defines the PSC as a collective security and early warning arrangement to facilitate timely and effective response to conflict and crisis situations in Africa. Other responsibilities conferred to the PSC by the protocol include prevention, management and resolution of conflicts, post-conflict peace building and developing common defence policies. The PSC has fifteen members elected on a regional basis by the Assembly. Similar in intent and operation to the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Security_Council" title="United Nations Security Council">United Nations Security Council</a>.</dd>
</dl>
<dl>
<dt><a href="/wiki/Economic,_Social_and_Cultural_Council" title="Economic, Social and Cultural Council">Economic, Social and Cultural Council</a></dt>
<dd>An advisory organ composed of professional and civic representatives, similar to the European <a href="/wiki/Economic_and_Social_Committee" title="Economic and Social Committee" class="mw-redirect">Economic and Social Committee</a>. The chair of ECOSOCC, elected in 2008, is Cameroonian lawyer <a href="/wiki/Akere_Muna" title="Akere Muna">Akere Muna</a> of the Pan-African Lawyers Union (PALU).</dd>
</dl>
<dl>
<dt><a href="/wiki/Specialised_Technical_Committees_of_the_African_Union" title="Specialised Technical Committees of the African Union">Specialised Technical Committees</a></dt>
<dd>Both the Abuja Treaty and the Constitutive Act provide for Specialised Technical Committees to be established made up of African ministers to advise the Assembly. In practice, they have never been set up. The ten proposed themes are: Rural Economy and Agricultural Matters; Monetary and Financial Affairs; Trade, Customs, and Immigration; Industry, Science and Technology; Energy, Natural Resources, and Environment; Transport, Communications, and Tourism; Health; Labour, and Social Affairs; Education, Culture, and Human Resources.</dd>
</dl>
<dl>
<dt>Financial institutions</dt>
</dl>
<ul>
<li><a href="/wiki/African_Central_Bank" title="African Central Bank">African Central Bank</a>&#160;– <a href="/wiki/Abuja" title="Abuja">Abuja</a>, Nigeria</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/African_Investment_Bank" title="African Investment Bank">African Investment Bank</a>&#160;– <a href="/wiki/Tripoli" title="Tripoli">Tripoli</a>, Libya</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/African_Monetary_Fund" title="African Monetary Fund">African Monetary Fund</a>&#160;– <a href="/wiki/Yaound%C3%A9" title="Yaoundé">Yaoundé</a>, Cameroon</li>
</ul>
<p>These institutions have not yet been established, however, the Steering Committees working on their founding have been constituted. Eventually, the AU aims to have a single currency (the <a href="/wiki/Afro_(currency)" title="Afro (currency)" class="mw-redirect">Afro</a>).</p>
<dl>
<dt>Human rights</dt>
<dd>The <a href="/wiki/African_Commission_on_Human_and_Peoples%27_Rights" title="African Commission on Human and Peoples' Rights">African Commission on Human and Peoples' Rights</a>, in existence since 1986, is established under the <a href="/wiki/African_Charter_on_Human_and_Peoples%27_Rights" title="African Charter on Human and Peoples' Rights">African Charter on Human and Peoples' Rights</a> (the African Charter) rather than the Constitutive Act of the African Union. It is the premier African human rights body, with responsibility for monitoring and promoting compliance with the African Charter. The <a href="/wiki/African_Court_on_Human_and_Peoples%27_Rights" title="African Court on Human and Peoples' Rights">African Court on Human and Peoples' Rights</a> was established in 2006 to supplement the work of the Commission, following the entry into force of a protocol to the African Charter providing for its creation. It is planned that the African Court on Human and Peoples' Rights will be merged with the African Court of Justice (see above).</dd>
</dl>
<dl>
<dt><a href="/wiki/African_Energy_Commission" title="African Energy Commission">African Energy Commission</a></dt>
</dl>

<dl>
<dt>ICC – Extraordinary Summit</dt>
<dd>Organized in <a href="/wiki/Addis_Ababa" title="Addis Ababa">Addis Ababa</a> from 10 to 16 October 2013, with the goal to discuss "Africa's relationship with the <a href="/wiki/International_Criminal_Court" title="International Criminal Court">ICC</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33"><span>[</span>33<span>]</span></a></sup> This was in regards to the ICC's non-adherence to AU calls to drop certain charges against sitting leaders and that it was disproportionally targeting Africans.<sup id="cite_ref-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-34"><span>[</span>34<span>]</span></a></sup></dd>
</dl>
<dl>

<dd>Organized in <a href="/wiki/Johannesburg" title="Johannesburg">Johannesburg</a> from 7 to 15 June 2015, with the theme "2015 year of women's empowerment and development towards Africa's agenda 2063".<sup id="cite_ref-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-41"><span>[</span>41<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42"><span>[</span>42<span>]</span></a></sup></dd>
</dl>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Role_of_the_diaspora">Role of the diaspora</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=African_Union&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Role of the diaspora">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>The Constitutive Act of the AU declares that it shall "invite and encourage the full participation of the <a href="/wiki/African_diaspora" title="African diaspora">African diaspora</a> as an important part of our Continent, in the building of the African Union". The African Union Government has defined the African diaspora as "consisting of people of African origin living outside the continent, irrespective of their citizenship and nationality and who are willing to contribute to the development of the continent and the building of the African Union".<sup id="cite_ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43"><span>[</span>43<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Current_issues">Current issues</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=African_Union&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Current issues">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>The AU faces many challenges, including health issues such as combating <a href="/wiki/Malaria" title="Malaria">malaria</a> and the AIDS/HIV epidemic; political issues such as confronting undemocratic regimes and mediating in the many civil wars; economic issues such as improving the <a href="/wiki/Human_Development_Index" title="Human Development Index">standard of living</a> of millions of impoverished, uneducated Africans; ecological issues such as dealing with recurring famines, <a href="/wiki/Desertification" title="Desertification">desertification</a>, and lack of ecological <a href="/wiki/Sustainability" title="Sustainability">sustainability</a>; as well as the <a href="/wiki/International_law" title="International law">legal</a> <a href="/wiki/Legal_status_of_Western_Sahara" title="Legal status of Western Sahara" class="mw-redirect">issues regarding Western Sahara</a>.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Union_Government">Union Government</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=African_Union&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Union Government">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The principal topic for debate at the July 2007 AU summit held in <a href="/wiki/Accra" title="Accra">Accra</a>, Ghana, was the creation of a Union Government,<sup id="cite_ref-44" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-44"><span>[</span>44<span>]</span></a></sup> with the aim of moving towards a <a href="/wiki/United_States_of_Africa" title="United States of Africa">United States of Africa</a>. A study on the <a href="/w/index.php?title=Union_Government_of_Africa&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Union Government of Africa (page does not exist)">Union Government</a> was adopted in late 2006,<sup id="cite_ref-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-45"><span>[</span>45<span>]</span></a></sup> and proposes various options for "completing" the African Union project. There are divisions among African states on the proposals, with some (notably <a href="/wiki/Great_Socialist_People%27s_Libyan_Arab_Jamahiriya" title="Great Socialist People's Libyan Arab Jamahiriya" class="mw-redirect">Libya</a>) following a maximalist view leading to a common government with an AU army; and others (especially the southern African states) supporting rather a strengthening of the existing structures, with some reforms to deal with administrative and political challenges in making the AU Commission and other bodies truly effective.<sup id="cite_ref-46" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-46"><span>[</span>46<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Following a heated debate in Accra, the <a href="/wiki/Assembly_of_the_African_Union" title="Assembly of the African Union">Assembly of Heads of State and Government</a> agreed in the form of a declaration to review the state of affairs of the AU with a view to determining its readiness towards a Union Government.<sup id="cite_ref-47" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-47"><span>[</span>47<span>]</span></a></sup> In particular, the Assembly agreed to:</p>
<ul>
<li>Accelerate the economic and political integration of the African continent, including the formation of a <a href="/w/index.php?title=Union_Government_of_Africa&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Union Government of Africa (page does not exist)">Union Government of Africa</a>;</li>
<li>Conduct an audit of the institutions and organs of the AU; review the relationship between the AU and the RECs; find ways to strengthen the AU and elaborate a timeframe to establish a Union Government of Africa.</li>
</ul>
<p>The declaration lastly noted the "importance of involving the African peoples, including Africans in the Diaspora, in the processes leading to the formation of the Union Government."</p>
<p>Following this decision, a panel of eminent persons was set up to conduct the "audit review". The review team began its work on 1 September 2007. The review was presented to the Assembly of Heads of State and Government at the January 2008 summit in Addis Ababa. No final decision was taken on the recommendations, however, and a committee of ten heads of state was appointed to consider the review and report back to the July 2008 summit to be held in Egypt.<sup id="cite_ref-48" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-48"><span>[</span>48<span>]</span></a></sup> At the July 2008 summit, a decision was once again deferred, for a "final" debate at the January 2009 summit to be held in Addis Ababa.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Role_of_Regional_Economic_Communities">Role of Regional Economic Communities</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=African_Union&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Role of Regional Economic Communities">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
