<a href="/wiki/Euler_diagram" title="Euler diagram">Euler diagram</a> showing the relationships between various multinational African organisations.<span style="float:right; font-weight:normal; font-size:xx-small;"><a href="/wiki/Template:Supranational_African_Bodies" title="Template:Supranational African Bodies"><span title="View this template">v</span></a> • <a href="/wiki/Template_talk:Supranational_African_Bodies" title="Template talk:Supranational African Bodies"><span title="Discuss this template">d</span></a> • <a class="external text" href="http://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Template:Supranational_African_Bodies&amp;action=edit"><span title="Edit this template" style=";">e</span></a></span></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>One of the key debates in relation to the achievement of greater continental integration is the relative priority that should be given to integration of the continent as a unit in itself or to integration of the sub-regions. The 1980 <a href="/wiki/Lagos_Plan_of_Action_for_the_Development_of_Africa" title="Lagos Plan of Action for the Development of Africa" class="mw-redirect">Lagos Plan of Action for the Development of Africa</a> and the 1991 treaty to establish the African Economic Community (also referred to as the Abuja Treaty), proposed the creation of <a href="/wiki/Regional_Economic_Communities" title="Regional Economic Communities">Regional Economic Communities</a> (RECs) as the basis for African integration, with a timetable for regional and then continental integration to follow.<sup id="cite_ref-49" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-49"><span>[</span>49<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Currently, there are eight RECs recognised by the AU, each established under a separate regional treaty. They are:</p>
<ul>
<li>the <a href="/wiki/Arab_Maghreb_Union" title="Arab Maghreb Union">Arab Maghreb Union</a> (UMA)</li>
<li>the <a href="/wiki/Common_Market_for_Eastern_and_Southern_Africa" title="Common Market for Eastern and Southern Africa">Common Market for Eastern and Southern Africa</a> (COMESA)</li>
<li>the <a href="/wiki/Community_of_Sahel-Saharan_States" title="Community of Sahel-Saharan States">Community of Sahel-Saharan States</a> (CEN-SAD)</li>
<li>the <a href="/wiki/East_African_Community" title="East African Community">East African Community</a> (EAC)</li>
<li>the <a href="/wiki/Economic_Community_of_Central_African_States" title="Economic Community of Central African States">Economic Community of Central African States</a> (ECCAS)</li>
<li>the <a href="/wiki/Economic_Community_of_West_African_States" title="Economic Community of West African States">Economic Community of West African States</a> (ECOWAS)</li>
<li>the <a href="/wiki/Intergovernmental_Authority_on_Development" title="Intergovernmental Authority on Development">Intergovernmental Authority on Development</a> (IGAD)</li>
<li>the <a href="/wiki/Southern_Africa_Development_Community" title="Southern Africa Development Community" class="mw-redirect">Southern Africa Development Community</a> (SADC)</li>
</ul>
<p>The membership of many of the communities overlaps, and their rationalisation has been under discussion for several years&#160;– and formed the theme of the 2006 Banjul summit. At the July 2007 Accra summit the Assembly finally decided to adopt a Protocol on Relations between the African Union and the Regional Economic Communities.<sup id="cite_ref-50" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-50"><span>[</span>50<span>]</span></a></sup> This protocol is intended to facilitate the harmonisation of policies and ensure compliance with the Abuja Treaty and Lagos Plan of Action time frames.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Selection_of_chair">Selection of chair</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=African_Union&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Selection of chair">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In 2006, the AU decided to create a Committee "to consider the implementation of a rotation system between the regions" in relation to the presidency. Controversy arose at the 2006 summit when Sudan announced its candidacy for the AU's chairmanship, as a representative of the East African region. Several member states refused to support Sudan because of tensions over <a href="/wiki/Darfur" title="Darfur">Darfur</a> (see also below). Sudan ultimately withdrew its candidacy and President <a href="/wiki/Denis_Sassou-Nguesso" title="Denis Sassou-Nguesso" class="mw-redirect">Denis Sassou-Nguesso</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Republic_of_the_Congo" title="Republic of the Congo">Republic of the Congo</a> was elected to a one-year term. At the January 2007 summit, Sassou-Nguesso was replaced by President <a href="/wiki/John_Agyekum_Kufuor" title="John Agyekum Kufuor" class="mw-redirect">John Agyekum Kufuor</a> of Ghana, despite another attempt by Sudan to gain the chair. 2007 was the 50th anniversary of Ghana's independence, a symbolic moment for the country to hold the chair of the AU—and to host the mid-year summit at which the proposed Union Government was also discussed. In January 2008, President <a href="/wiki/Jakaya_Kikwete" title="Jakaya Kikwete">Jakaya Kikwete</a> of Tanzania took over as chair, representing the East African region and thus apparently ending Sudan's attempt to become chair—at least till the rotation returns to East Africa.<sup id="cite_ref-51" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-51"><span>[</span>51<span>]</span></a></sup> The current chair is Benin.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="AIDS_in_Africa">AIDS in Africa</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=African_Union&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: AIDS in Africa">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>One of the most serious issues to face Africa is not a dispute between nations, but rather the rapid spread of HIV and the AIDS <a href="/wiki/Pandemic" title="Pandemic">pandemic</a>. <a href="/wiki/Sub-Saharan_Africa" title="Sub-Saharan Africa">Sub-Saharan Africa</a>, especially southern Africa, is by far the most affected area in the world, and the infection is now starting to claim lives by the millions. While the measurement of HIV prevalence rates has proved methodologically challenging, more than 20% of the sexually active population of many countries of southern Africa may be infected, with South Africa, Botswana, <a href="/wiki/Kenya" title="Kenya">Kenya</a>, Namibia, and <a href="/wiki/Zimbabwe" title="Zimbabwe">Zimbabwe</a> all expected to have a decrease in <a href="/wiki/Life_expectancy" title="Life expectancy">life expectancy</a> by an average of 6.5 years. The effects on South Africa, which constitutes 30% of the AU's economy,<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (March 2010)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> threatens to significantly stunt GDP growth, and thus internal and external trade for the continent.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Libya">Libya</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=African_Union&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Libya">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The AU attempted to mediate in the early stages of the <a href="/wiki/2011_Libyan_civil_war" title="2011 Libyan civil war" class="mw-redirect">2011 Libyan civil war</a>, forming an <i>ad hoc</i> committee of five presidents (<a href="/wiki/Republic_of_the_Congo" title="Republic of the Congo">Congolese</a> President <a href="/wiki/Denis_Sassou_Nguesso" title="Denis Sassou Nguesso">Denis Sassou Nguesso</a>, Malian President <a href="/wiki/Amadou_Toumani_Tour%C3%A9" title="Amadou Toumani Touré">Amadou Toumani Touré</a>, Mauritanian President <a href="/wiki/Mohamed_Ould_Abdel_Aziz" title="Mohamed Ould Abdel Aziz">Mohamed Ould Abdel Aziz</a>, South African President <a href="/wiki/Jacob_Zuma" title="Jacob Zuma">Jacob Zuma</a>, and Ugandan President <a href="/wiki/Yoweri_Museveni" title="Yoweri Museveni">Yoweri Museveni</a>) to broker a truce.<sup id="cite_ref-52" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-52"><span>[</span>52<span>]</span></a></sup> However, the beginning of the <a href="/wiki/NATO" title="NATO">NATO</a>-led <a href="/wiki/2011_military_intervention_in_Libya" title="2011 military intervention in Libya">military intervention</a> in March 2011 prevented the committee from traveling to <a href="/wiki/Great_Socialist_People%27s_Libyan_Arab_Jamahiriya" title="Great Socialist People's Libyan Arab Jamahiriya" class="mw-redirect">Libya</a> to meet with Libyan leader and former head of the AU until 2010 <a href="/wiki/Muammar_Gaddafi" title="Muammar Gaddafi">Muammar Gaddafi</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-53" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-53"><span>[</span>53<span>]</span></a></sup> As a body, the AU sharply dissented from the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Security_Council" title="United Nations Security Council">United Nations Security Council</a>'s decision to create a <a href="/wiki/No-fly_zone" title="No-fly zone">no-fly zone</a> over Libya,<sup id="cite_ref-54" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-54"><span>[</span>54<span>]</span></a></sup> though a few member states, such as <a href="/wiki/Botswana" title="Botswana">Botswana</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-55" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-55"><span>[</span>55<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Gabon" title="Gabon">Gabon</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-56" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-56"><span>[</span>56<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Zambia" title="Zambia">Zambia</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-57" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-57"><span>[</span>57<span>]</span></a></sup> and others expressed support for <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Security_Council_Resolution_1973" title="United Nations Security Council Resolution 1973">the resolution</a>.</p>
<p>As a result of Gaddafi's defeat at the <a href="/wiki/2011_Battle_of_Tripoli" title="2011 Battle of Tripoli" class="mw-redirect">Battle of Tripoli</a>, the decisive battle of the war, in August 2011, the <a href="/wiki/Arab_League" title="Arab League">Arab League</a> voted to recognise the anti-Gaddafi <a href="/wiki/National_Transitional_Council" title="National Transitional Council">National Transitional Council</a> as the legitimate government of the country pending elections,<sup id="cite_ref-58" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-58"><span>[</span>58<span>]</span></a></sup> yet although the council has been recognised by several AU member states, including two countries that are also members of the Arab League,<sup id="cite_ref-59" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-59"><span>[</span>59<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-60" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-60"><span>[</span>60<span>]</span></a></sup> the AU <a href="/wiki/Peace_and_Security_Council" title="Peace and Security Council">Peace and Security Council</a> voted on 26 August 2011 not to recognise it, insisting that a ceasefire be agreed to and a national <a href="/wiki/Unity_government" title="Unity government" class="mw-redirect">unity government</a> be formed by both sides in the civil war.<sup id="cite_ref-61" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-61"><span>[</span>61<span>]</span></a></sup> A number of AU member states led by <a href="/wiki/Ethiopia" title="Ethiopia">Ethiopia</a>, Nigeria, and <a href="/wiki/Rwanda" title="Rwanda">Rwanda</a> requested that the AU recognise the NTC as Libya's interim governing authority,<sup id="cite_ref-62" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-62"><span>[</span>62<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-63" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-63"><span>[</span>63<span>]</span></a></sup> and several other AU member states have recognised the NTC regardless of the Peace and Security Council's decision.<sup id="cite_ref-64" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-64"><span>[</span>64<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-65" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-65"><span>[</span>65<span>]</span></a></sup> However, AU member states <a href="/wiki/Algeria" title="Algeria">Algeria</a><sup id="cite_ref-66" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-66"><span>[</span>66<span>]</span></a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Zimbabwe" title="Zimbabwe">Zimbabwe</a><sup id="cite_ref-67" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-67"><span>[</span>67<span>]</span></a></sup> have indicated they will not recognise the NTC, and South Africa has expressed reservations as well.<sup id="cite_ref-68" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-68"><span>[</span>68<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>On 20 September 2011, the African Union officially recognised the National Transitional Council as the legitimate representative of Libya.<sup id="cite_ref-69" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-69"><span>[</span>69<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Interventions_in_support_of_constitutionality">Interventions in support of constitutionality</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=African_Union&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Interventions in support of constitutionality">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Mali">Mali</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=African_Union&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Mali">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<table class="metadata plainlinks ambox mbox-small-left ambox-content" role="presentation">
<tr>
<td class="mbox-image"><a href="/wiki/File:Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg" class="image"><img alt="[icon]" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1c/Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg/20px-Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg.png" width="20" height="14" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1c/Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg/30px-Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1c/Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg/40px-Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="44" data-file-height="31" /></a></td>
<td class="mbox-text"><span class="mbox-text-span">This section requires <a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=African_Union&amp;action=edit">expansion</a>. <small><i>(July 2013)</i></small></span></td>
</tr>
</table>
<p>In March 2012, a military coup was staged in Mali, when an alliance of Touareg and Islamist forces conquered the north, resulting in a coming to power of the Islamists. After a military intervention with help from French troops, the region was in control of the Malian army. To reinstall local authorities, the AU helped to form a caretaker government, supporting it and holding presidential elections in Mali in July 2013.<sup id="cite_ref-dandc.eu_70-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-dandc.eu-70"><span>[</span>70<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Mauritania">Mauritania</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=African_Union&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Mauritania">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>On 3 August 2005, a coup in <a href="/wiki/Mauritania" title="Mauritania">Mauritania</a> led the African Union to suspend the country from all organisational activities. The Military Council that took control of Mauritania promised to hold elections within two years.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (July 2011)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> These were held in early 2007, the first time that the country had held elections that were generally agreed to be of an acceptable standard. Following the elections, Mauritania's membership of the AU was restored. However, on 6 August 2008, a fresh coup overthrew the government elected in 2007. The AU once again suspended Mauritania from the continental body.<sup id="cite_ref-71" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-71"><span>[</span>71<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Togo">Togo</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=African_Union&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Togo">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In response to the death of <a href="/wiki/Gnassingb%C3%A9_Eyad%C3%A9ma" title="Gnassingbé Eyadéma">Gnassingbé Eyadéma</a>, President of <a href="/wiki/Togo" title="Togo">Togo</a>, on 5 February 2005, AU leaders described the naming of his son <a href="/wiki/Faure_Gnassingb%C3%A9" title="Faure Gnassingbé">Faure Gnassingbé</a> the successor as a <a href="/wiki/Coup_d%27%C3%A9tat" title="Coup d'état">military coup</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-72" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-72"><span>[</span>72<span>]</span></a></sup> Togo's constitution calls for the speaker of parliament to succeed the president in the event of his death. By law, the parliament speaker must call national elections to choose a new president within sixty days. The AU's protest forced Gnassingbé to hold elections. Under heavy allegations of election fraud, he was officially elected President on 4 May 2005.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Regional_conflicts_and_military_interventions">Regional conflicts and military interventions</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=African_Union&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Regional conflicts and military interventions">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>One of the objectives of the AU is to "promote peace, security, and stability on the continent".<sup id="cite_ref-73" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-73"><span>[</span>73<span>]</span></a></sup> Among its principles is 'Peaceful resolution of conflicts among Member States of the Union through such appropriate means as may be decided upon by the Assembly'.<sup id="cite_ref-74" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-74"><span>[</span>74<span>]</span></a></sup> The primary body charged with implementing these objectives and principles is the Peace and Security Council. The PSC has the power, among other things, to authorise peace support missions, to impose sanctions in case of unconstitutional change of government, and to "take initiatives and action it deems appropriate" in response to potential or actual conflicts. The PSC is a decision-making body in its own right, and its decisions are binding on member states.</p>
<p>Article 4(h) of the Constitutive Act, repeated in article 4 of the Protocol to the Constitutive Act on the PSC, also recognises the right of the Union to intervene in member state in circumstances of war crimes, genocide and crimes against humanity. Any decision to intervene in a member state under article 4 of the Constitutive Act will be made by the Assembly on the recommendation of the PSC.</p>
<p>Since it first met in 2004, the PSC has been active in relation to the crises in Darfur, Comoros, Somalia, <a href="/wiki/Democratic_Republic_of_Congo" title="Democratic Republic of Congo" class="mw-redirect">Democratic Republic of Congo</a>, Burundi, Côte d'Ivoire and other countries. It has adopted resolutions creating the AU peacekeeping operations in Somalia and Darfur, and imposing sanctions against persons undermining peace and security (such as travel bans and asset freezes against the leaders of the rebellion in Comoros). The Council is in the process of overseeing the establishment of a "standby force" to serve as a permanent African peacekeeping force.,<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (January 2014)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> Institute for Security Studies, South Africa, March 2008.</p>
<p>The founding treaty of the AU also called for the establishment of the African Peace and Security Architecture (APSA), including the <a href="/wiki/African_Standby_Force" title="African Standby Force">African Standby Force</a> (ASF), which is to be deployed in emergencies. That means, in cases of genocide or other serious human-rights violations, an ASF mission can be launched even against the wishes of the government of the country concerned, as long as it is approved by the AU General Assembly. In the past AU peacekeeping missions, the concept was not yet applied, forces had to be mobilised from member states. The AU is planning on putting the concept into practise by 2015 the earliest.<sup id="cite_ref-dandc.eu_70-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-dandc.eu-70"><span>[</span>70<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Darfur.2C_Sudan">Darfur, Sudan</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=African_Union&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Darfur, Sudan">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">Main article: <a href="/wiki/African_Union_Mission_in_Sudan" title="African Union Mission in Sudan">African Union Mission in Sudan</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Eritrea_-_Flickr_-_Al_Jazeera_English.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c0/Eritrea_-_Flickr_-_Al_Jazeera_English.jpg/220px-Eritrea_-_Flickr_-_Al_Jazeera_English.jpg" width="220" height="146" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c0/Eritrea_-_Flickr_-_Al_Jazeera_English.jpg/330px-Eritrea_-_Flickr_-_Al_Jazeera_English.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c0/Eritrea_-_Flickr_-_Al_Jazeera_English.jpg/440px-Eritrea_-_Flickr_-_Al_Jazeera_English.jpg 2x" data-file-width="680" data-file-height="450" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Eritrea_-_Flickr_-_Al_Jazeera_English.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/South_Sudanese_independence_referendum,_2011" title="South Sudanese independence referendum, 2011">South Sudanese independence referendum, 2011</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>In response to the ongoing <a href="/wiki/Darfur_conflict" title="Darfur conflict" class="mw-redirect">Darfur conflict</a> in Sudan, the AU has deployed 7,000 peacekeepers, many from <a href="/wiki/Rwanda" title="Rwanda">Rwanda</a> and <a href="/wiki/Nigeria" title="Nigeria">Nigeria</a>, to <a href="/wiki/Darfur" title="Darfur">Darfur</a>. While a donor's conference in <a href="/wiki/Addis_Ababa" title="Addis Ababa">Addis Ababa</a> in 2005 helped raise funds to sustain the peacekeepers through that year and into 2006, in July 2006 the AU said it would pull out at the end of September when its mandate expires.<sup id="cite_ref-75" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-75"><span>[</span>75<span>]</span></a></sup> Critics of the AU peacekeepers, including Dr. <a href="/wiki/Eric_Reeves" title="Eric Reeves">Eric Reeves</a>, have said these forces are largely ineffective due to lack of funds, personnel, and expertise. Monitoring an area roughly the size of France has made it even more difficult to sustain an effective mission. In June 2006, the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Congress" title="United States Congress">United States Congress</a> appropriated US$173&#160;million for the AU force. Some, such as the <a href="/wiki/Genocide_Intervention_Network" title="Genocide Intervention Network">Genocide Intervention Network</a>, have called for United Nations (UN) or <a href="/wiki/NATO" title="NATO">NATO</a> intervention to augment and/or replace the AU peacekeepers. The UN has considered deploying a force, though it would not likely enter the country until at least October 2007.<sup id="cite_ref-76" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-76"><span>[</span>76<span>]</span></a></sup> The under-funded and badly equipped AU mission was set to expire on 31 December 2006 but was extended to 30 June 2007 and merged with the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_African_Union_Mission_in_Darfur" title="United Nations African Union Mission in Darfur" class="mw-redirect">United Nations African Union Mission in Darfur</a> in October 2007. In July 2009 the African Union ceased cooperation with the <a href="/wiki/International_Criminal_Court" title="International Criminal Court">International Criminal Court</a>, refusing to recognise the international arrest warrant it had issued against Sudan's leader, <a href="/wiki/Omar_al-Bashir" title="Omar al-Bashir">Omar al-Bashir</a>, who was indicted in 2008 for <a href="/wiki/War_crime" title="War crime">War crimes</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-77" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-77"><span>[</span>77<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>The AU struggled to have a strategic role in the independence talks and the reconciliation process of <a href="/wiki/South_Sudan" title="South Sudan">South Sudan</a>, anyway due to overwhelming interests of African and non-African powers, its influence is still limited and not consistent.<sup id="cite_ref-78" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-78"><span>[</span>78<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Somalia">Somalia</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=African_Union&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Somalia">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">Main article: <a href="/wiki/African_Union_Mission_to_Somalia" title="African Union Mission to Somalia">African Union Mission to Somalia</a></div>
<p>From the early 1990s up until 2012, <a href="/wiki/Somalia" title="Somalia">Somalia</a> was without a functioning central government. A peace agreement aimed at ending the <a href="/wiki/Somali_Civil_War" title="Somali Civil War">civil war</a> that broke out following the collapse of the <a href="/wiki/Siad_Barre" title="Siad Barre">Siad Barre</a> regime was signed in 2006 after many years of peace talks. However, the new government was almost immediately threatened by further violence. To temporarily shore up the government's military base, starting in March 2007, AU soldiers began arriving in <a href="/wiki/Mogadishu" title="Mogadishu">Mogadishu</a> as part of a peacekeeping force that was intended by the AU to eventually be 8,000 strong.<sup id="cite_ref-79" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-79"><span>[</span>79<span>]</span></a></sup> Eritrea recalled its ambassadors to the African Union on 20 November 2009<sup id="cite_ref-80" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-80"><span>[</span>80<span>]</span></a></sup> after the African Union called on the United Nations Security Council to impose sanctions on them due to their alleged support of Somali Islamists attempting to topple the <a href="/wiki/Transitional_Federal_Government" title="Transitional Federal Government">Transitional Federal Government</a> of Somalia, the internationally recognised government of Somalia which holds Somalia's seat on the African Union.<sup id="cite_ref-81" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-81"><span>[</span>81<span>]</span></a></sup> On 22 December 2009, the Security Council passed <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Security_Council_Resolution_1907" title="United Nations Security Council Resolution 1907">UNSCR 1907</a>, which imposed an arms embargo on Eritrea, travel bans on Eritrean leaders, and asset freezes on Eritrean officials. Eritrea strongly criticised the resolution. In January 2011, Eritrea reestablished their mission to the AU in Addis Ababa.<sup id="cite_ref-82" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-82"><span>[</span>82<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Anjouan.2C_Comoros">Anjouan, Comoros</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=African_Union&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Anjouan, Comoros">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">Main article: <a href="/wiki/2008_invasion_of_Anjouan" title="2008 invasion of Anjouan">2008 invasion of Anjouan</a></div>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Economy">Economy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=African_Union&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Economy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Economy_of_the_African_Union" title="Economy of the African Union">Economy of the African Union</a></div>
<p>The AU's future goals include the creation of a <a href="/wiki/Free_trade_area" title="Free trade area">free trade area</a>, a <a href="/wiki/Customs_union" title="Customs union">customs union</a>, a <a href="/wiki/Single_market" title="Single market">single market</a>, a <a href="/wiki/Central_bank" title="Central bank">central bank</a>, and a common currency (see <a href="/wiki/African_Monetary_Union" title="African Monetary Union">African Monetary Union</a>), thereby establishing <a href="/wiki/Economic_and_monetary_union" title="Economic and monetary union">economic and monetary union</a>. The current plan is to establish an <a href="/wiki/African_Economic_Community" title="African Economic Community">African Economic Community</a> with a single currency by 2023.<sup id="cite_ref-83" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-83"><span>[</span>83<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Languages">Languages</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=African_Union&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Languages">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Languages_of_the_African_Union" title="Languages of the African Union">Languages of the African Union</a></div>
<p>According to the Constitutive Act of the African Union, its working languages are Arabic, English, French and Portuguese, and <a href="/wiki/Languages_of_Africa" title="Languages of Africa">African languages</a> "if possible".<sup id="cite_ref-84" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-84"><span>[</span>84<span>]</span></a></sup> A protocol amending the Constitutive Act, adopted in 2003 but as of 2015 not in force, would add Spanish, <a href="/wiki/Swahili_language" title="Swahili language">Swahili</a> and "any other African language" and declare all "official" (rather than "working") languages of the African Union.<sup id="cite_ref-85" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-85"><span>[</span>85<span>]</span></a></sup> The Executive Council shall determine the process and practical modalities for the use of official languages as working languages.</p>
<p>Founded in 2001 under the auspices of the AU, the <a href="/wiki/African_Academy_of_Languages" title="African Academy of Languages">African Academy of Languages</a> promotes the usage and perpetuation of African languages among African people. The AU declared 2006 the Year of African Languages.<sup id="cite_ref-Year_of_African_Languages_86-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Year_of_African_Languages-86"><span>[</span>86<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Year_of_African_Languages_2_87-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Year_of_African_Languages_2-87"><span>[</span>87<span>]</span></a></sup> 2006 also marked Ghana's 55th anniversary since it founded the <a href="/wiki/Bureau_of_Ghana_Languages" title="Bureau of Ghana Languages">Bureau of Ghana Languages</a> originally known as <a href="/wiki/Bureau_of_Ghana_Languages" title="Bureau of Ghana Languages">Gold Coast Vernacular Literature Bureau</a>.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Geography">Geography</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=African_Union&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Geography">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Geography_of_the_African_Union" title="Geography of the African Union">Geography of the African Union</a></div>
<p>Member <a href="/wiki/Sovereign_state" title="Sovereign state">states</a> of the African Union cover almost the entirety of continental Africa and several off-shore islands. Consequently, the geography of the African Union is wildly diverse, including the world's largest hot desert (the <a href="/wiki/Sahara" title="Sahara">Sahara</a>), huge jungles and <a href="/wiki/Savanna" title="Savanna">savannas</a>, and the world's longest river (the <a href="/wiki/Nile" title="Nile">Nile</a>).</p>
<p>The AU presently has an area of 29,922,059&#160;km² (18,592,705&#160;mi²), with 24,165&#160;km (15,015&#160;mi) of coastline. The vast majority of this area is on continental Africa, while the only significant territory off the mainland is the island of <a href="/wiki/Madagascar" title="Madagascar">Madagascar</a> (<a href="/wiki/List_of_islands_by_area" title="List of islands by area">the world's fourth largest island</a>), accounting for slightly less than 2% of the total.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Foreign_relations">Foreign relations</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=African_Union&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Foreign relations">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Foreign_relations_of_the_African_Union" title="Foreign relations of the African Union">Foreign relations of the African Union</a></div>
<p>The individual member states of the African Union coordinate foreign policy through this agency, in addition to conducting their own <a href="/wiki/International_relations" title="International relations">international relations</a> on a state-by-state basis. The AU represents the interests of African peoples at large in <a href="/wiki/Intergovernmental_organisation" title="Intergovernmental organisation" class="mw-redirect">intergovernmental organisations</a> (IGOs); for instance, it is a <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_General_Assembly_observers" title="United Nations General Assembly observers">permanent observer</a> at the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_General_Assembly" title="United Nations General Assembly">United Nations General Assembly</a>. Both the African Union and the United Nations work in tandem to address issues of common concerns in various areas. The African Union Mission in United Nations aspires to serve as a bridge between the two Organisations.</p>
<p>Membership of the AU overlaps with other IGOs and occasionally these third-party organisations and the AU will coordinate matters of public policy. The African Union maintains special diplomatic representation with the <a href="/wiki/Ambassadors_from_the_United_States" title="Ambassadors from the United States" class="mw-redirect">United States</a> and the <a href="/wiki/European_Union_Special_Representative" title="European Union Special Representative">European Union</a>.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=African_Union&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">Main article: <a href="/wiki/History_of_the_African_Union" title="History of the African Union">History of the African Union</a></div>
<p>The historical foundations of the African Union originated in the <a href="/wiki/Union_of_African_States" title="Union of African States">Union of African States</a>, an early <a href="/wiki/Confederation" title="Confederation">confederation</a> that was established by <a href="/wiki/Kwame_Nkrumah" title="Kwame Nkrumah">Kwame Nkrumah</a> in the 1960s, as well as subsequent attempts to unite Africa, including the <a href="/wiki/Organisation_of_African_Unity" title="Organisation of African Unity">Organisation of African Unity</a> (OAU), which was established on 25 May 1963, and the <a href="/wiki/African_Economic_Community" title="African Economic Community">African Economic Community</a> in 1981. Critics argued that the OAU in particular did little to protect the rights and liberties of African citizens from their own political leaders, often dubbing it the "Dictators' Club".<sup id="cite_ref-88" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-88"><span>[</span>88<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>The idea of creating the AU was revived in the mid-1990s under the leadership of Libyan head of state <a href="/wiki/Muammar_al-Gaddafi" title="Muammar al-Gaddafi" class="mw-redirect">Muammar al-Gaddafi</a>: the heads of state and government of the OAU issued the <a href="/wiki/Sirte_Declaration" title="Sirte Declaration">Sirte Declaration</a> (named after Sirte, in Libya) on 9 September 1999, calling for the establishment of an African Union. The Declaration was followed by summits at <a href="/wiki/Lom%C3%A9" title="Lomé">Lomé</a> in 2000, when the <a href="/wiki/Constitutive_Act_of_the_African_Union" title="Constitutive Act of the African Union">Constitutive Act of the African Union</a> was adopted, and at <a href="/wiki/Lusaka" title="Lusaka">Lusaka</a> in 2001, when the plan for the implementation of the African Union was adopted. During the same period, the initiative for the establishment of the <a href="/wiki/New_Partnership_for_Africa%27s_Development" title="New Partnership for Africa's Development">New Partnership for Africa's Development</a> (NEPAD), was also established.</p>
<p>The African Union was launched in <a href="/wiki/Durban" title="Durban">Durban</a> on 9 July 2002, by its first chairperson, South African <a href="/wiki/Thabo_Mbeki" title="Thabo Mbeki">Thabo Mbeki</a>, at the first session of the Assembly of the African Union. The second session of the Assembly was in <a href="/wiki/Maputo" title="Maputo">Maputo</a> in 2003, and the third session in <a href="/wiki/Addis_Ababa" title="Addis Ababa">Addis Ababa</a> on 6 July 2004.</p>
<p><a href="/wiki/Barack_Obama" title="Barack Obama">Barack Obama</a> was the first ever sitting <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">United States</a> president to speak in front of the African Union in Addis Ababa, on 29 July 2015. With his speech, he encouraged the world to increase economic ties via investments and trade with the <a href="/wiki/Outline_of_Africa" title="Outline of Africa">continent</a>, and lauded the progresses made in <a href="/wiki/Education_in_Africa" title="Education in Africa">education</a>, infrastructure and <a href="/wiki/Economy_of_Africa" title="Economy of Africa">economy</a>. But he also criticized lacks of democracy and leaders who refuse to step off, discrimination against minorities (<a href="/wiki/LGBT" title="LGBT">LGBT</a> people, religious groups and ethnicities) and corruption. He suggested an intensified <a href="/wiki/Democratization" title="Democratization">democratization</a> and free trade, to significantly increase living quality for Africans.<sup id="cite_ref-89" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-89"><span>[</span>89<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-90" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-90"><span>[</span>90<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Symbols">Symbols</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=African_Union&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: Symbols">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Emblem_of_the_African_Union.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/f/f5/Emblem_of_the_African_Union.svg/200px-Emblem_of_the_African_Union.svg.png" width="200" height="179" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/f/f5/Emblem_of_the_African_Union.svg/300px-Emblem_of_the_African_Union.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/f/f5/Emblem_of_the_African_Union.svg/400px-Emblem_of_the_African_Union.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="145" data-file-height="130" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Emblem_of_the_African_Union.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<center><b>Emblem of the African Union</b></center>
</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Emblem_of_the_African_Union" title="Emblem of the African Union">emblem of the African Union</a> consists of a gold ribbon bearing small interlocking red rings, from which palm leaves shoot up around an outer gold circle and an inner green circle, within which is a gold representation of Africa. The red interlinked rings stand for African solidarity and the blood shed for the liberation of Africa; the palm leaves for peace; the gold, for Africa's wealth and bright future; the green, for African hopes and aspirations. To symbolise African unity, the silhouette of Africa is drawn without internal borders.</p>
<p>The African Union adopted its new flag at its 14th Ordinary Session of the Assembly of Heads of State and Government taking place in Addis Ababa 2010. During the 8th African Union Summit which took place in Addis Ababa on 29 and 30 January 2007, the Heads of State and Government decided to launch a competition for the selection of a new flag for the Union. They prescribed a green background for the flag symbolising hope of Africa and stars to represent Member States.</p>
<p>Pursuant to this decision, the African Union Commission (AUC) organised a competition for the selection of a new flag for the African Union. The AUC received a total of 106 entries proposed by citizens of 19 African countries and 2 from the Diaspora. The proposals were then examined by a panel of experts put in place by the African Union Commission and selected from the five African regions for short listing according to the main directions given by the Heads of State and Government.</p>
<p>At the 13th Ordinary Session of the Assembly, the Heads of State and Government examined the report of the Panel and selected one among all the proposals. The flag is now part of the paraphernalia of the African Union and replaces the old one.</p>
<p>The old <a href="/wiki/Flag_of_the_African_Union" title="Flag of the African Union">flag of the African Union</a> bears a broad green horizontal stripe, a narrow band of gold, the emblem of the African Union at the centre of a broad white stripe, another narrow gold band and a final broad green stripe. Again, the green and gold symbolise Africa's hopes and aspirations as well as its wealth and bright future, and the white represents the purity of Africa's desire for friends throughout the world. The flag has led to the creation of the "<a href="/wiki/National_colours" title="National colours">national colours</a>" of Africa of gold and green (sometimes together with white). These colours are visible in one way or another in the flags of many African nations. Together the colours green, gold, and red constitute the <a href="/wiki/Pan-African_colours" title="Pan-African colours">Pan-African colours</a>.</p>
<p>The African Union has adopted a new anthem, <i><a href="/wiki/Let_Us_All_Unite_and_Celebrate_Together" title="Let Us All Unite and Celebrate Together">Let Us All Unite and Celebrate Together</a></i>, and has the chorus <i>O sons and daughters of Africa, flesh of the sun and flesh of the sky, Let us make Africa the tree of life</i>.</p>

<li><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.africa-union.org/root/AU/Conferences/2008/june/summit/summit.htm">11th AU summit July 2008</a>, Sharm El Sheikh, Egypt</li>
